According to al-Attar, why is the independent section (اسم/فعل) presented before the particle in the division of المفرد?
A) Because it is more common in speech.
B) Because its concept is existential, and the negation is posterior.
C) Because it is more important for grammar.
D) Because it was mentioned first by the author.

Key Takeaway
The division of single words into noun, verb, and particle hinges on whether they can convey a complete meaning independently for predication, but this rule has exceptions like deficient verbs which may be treated as particles.

?
Consider the verb 'ليس'. Is it independent? What does the passage say about deficient verbs? Would 'ليس' be considered a particle? Why or why not?

What Is Mantiq?
advanced
15 min
Refining the Definition of Istiqlal (Independence) in Logical Parts of Speech
Author refines the definition of istiqlal (independence) for meanings of particles, verbs, and nouns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the refined definition of istiqlal (independence) as conceptual self-sufficiency and apply it to distinguish nouns, verbs, and particles in logic.

Core Idea
Istiqlal is not predication ability; it is meaning observed for itself.

In this passage, al-Dasūqī refines the definition of istiqlal (independence) by distinguishing the cause (conceptual self-sufficiency) from its effect (predication). He engages with earlier commentaries to clarify that a word's meaning is independent when it is observed essentially, not as a follower of another. This refined understanding resolves ambiguities in classifying parts of speech in logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being refined
Find where the author discusses istiqlal. Note that it is a real attribute (wasf haqiqi) of meaning.
2
Extract the core definition
The author states: 'الاستقلال وصف حقيقي للمعنى، ومعناه أن يكون ملحوظاً مقصوداً بالذات لا بتبعيَّة أمر آخر'. This means independence is that the meaning is observed as intended essentially, not as a follower.
This is the key sentence.
3
Distinguish predication from independence
The author clarifies that predication (al-ikhbār bihi) is a necessary consequence (lāzim) of independence, not its essence. Many mistakenly think independence is defined by predication ability.
Reflect on the commentator's lenient phrasing 'is independent in predication' – it is a metaphor.
4
Apply the definition to parts of speech
Using the refined definition, nouns and verbs are independent (their meanings are intended essentially), while particles (adawāt) are not (they are observations for other things).
Note the difference between logicians and grammarians: for logicians, the verb itself is the predicate and independent; for grammarians, it needs a pronoun.

الحرفِ موجودٌ فيهِ، لكن لا يُفهم بدونِ ذكرِ المتعلّق، وقِيلَ: إِنَّ مَعنى الحرفِ موجود في كل من الحرفِ والمتعلّقِ، فَلَا يعقل إلا بمجموع الأمرين، وإِنَّما قُيّد بوحده ؛ لأنَّ الحرفَ يُخبرُ بِهِ مع غيره نحو : زيد في الدار.
إنْ قُلْتَ: الفعلُ لا يخبرُ بِهِ وحدَهُ بل مع فاعله ؛ قُلْتُ : هذا مذهبُ النُّحاة؛ لأنَّهم ينظرونَ لِلألفاظ، فَلَا بُدَّ من ضمير في الخبر إذا كان فعلاً يعود على المبتدأ ؛ لأجل ربط الكلام، أو ما يقومُ مقامَ الضَّميرِ ، وأمَّا المناطقةُ؛ فالخبر عندَهم نَفْسُ الفعل ؛ لأنَّهم إنَّما يلتفتونَ للمعاني، والمثبتُ للمبتدأ هو معنى الفعل، تأمل. فإنْ قُلْتَ : مَا نكتةُ قولِ الشَّارح: استقلَّ بِالإخبار به وحده، ولم يقل عنه؟ ؛ قُلْتُ : لأنَّ المصنِّف جعلَ المفردَ مُقَسَّماً لِمَا يخبرُ بِهِ؛ لَا لِمَا يخبرُ عنه
العطار • الأدوات إلى غيرِ زمانيَّةٍ وزمانيَّةٍ، وَهِيَ الأفعالُ النَّاقصةُ، غايةُ مَا في البابِ أَنَّ اصطلاحهم لا يوافق اصطلاحَ النُّحاةِ، وذلك غيرُ لازم ا.هـ. ، وسيأتي لهذا الكلام تتمَّةٌ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الاستقلال وصفٌ حقيقي للمعنى، ومعناه أن يكونَ مَلحوظاً مقصوداً بالذَّاتِ لا بِتَبعيَّةِ أمرٍ آخَرَ بأنْ يكونَ مِرآة لملاحظةٍ غيرِهِ كالأدواتِ، وبتبعيَّةِ استقلال المعنى يصحُ الإخبارُ باللفظ ، وعنهُ فَمعنى قولِ الشَّارح : إن استقل بالإخبارِ بِهِ وحدَهُ ؛ إن استقلَّ مَعناه بسببِ صَلاحِيَّةِ لَفظِهِ لِلإخبارِ بِهِ وحدَهُ وهذهِ السَّببيَّةُ في العِلْم يعني عِلمنا أنَّ مَعناهُ مُستقل لكوننا وجدناهُ مُخبراً بِهِ لا يسببه في الاستقلال؛ لأنَّ الأمر بالعكس كَمَا سَمِعْتَ، فَكَلامُ الشَّارح مبني على المسامحة، فظهرَ اتِّجاهُ قَولِ المحشّي : الاستقلال حقيقةً هو استقلال المعنى بالمفهوميَّة، والإخبارُ بِهِ لَازِمٌ لِذلكَ فالأظهرُ أَنْ يُقالَ في شرح الكلامِ إن استقلَّ في الدَّلالةِ لِكُونِ مَعناهُ مُستقلا
فَمَعَ الدَّلَالَةِ بِهَيْئَتِهِ قَوْلُهُ : فَمَعَ الدَّلالةِ أي : بسبب الوضع، وإلا ؛ لخرجت الإنشاءات المنسلخة عن الزَّمانِ، كَبِعْتُ واشتريتُ قَوْلُهُ : فَمَعَ الدَّلَالَةِ بِهَيْئَتِهِ يرد عليه المضارع، فإنَّه لا يدلُّ على أحدها ، وإِنَّما يدلُّ على الحالِ والاستقبال . العطار وهي الملاحظة غير ملحوظ بتبعيَّةِ الغيرِ حتَّى لا يمكن ملاحظته بدونه ا . هـ . ، ا.هـ. ، وسقوط ما قِيلَ : إِنْ بَاءَ بالإخبارِ لِتَصوير الاستقلال، وأنَّ الشَّارِحَ حمل الاستقلال على مَا هُوَ رَاجِعُ لِلَّفْظِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ مُسايرةٌ للشَّارحِ فِي تَسَاهُلِهِ يؤيِّدُ مَا ذكرنا قولُ مير زاهد: إِنَّ مَناطَ الحُكْمِ على الملاحظةِ والتَّوجه بالذَّاتِ، فَلَمَّا كانَتِ الأسماء والكلمات ملحوظة بالذَّاتِ، والأداةُ مَلحوظةً بِالعَرَضِ ؛ صَحَ الحُكْمُ فيهما ولمْ يصح فيها ا.هـ. قَوْلُهُ : فَمَعَ الدَّلَالَةِ إِنْ أُريدَ وغير المستقل ؛ غيرُ مُستقلِّ، وإنْ أُريدَ مَا هو أعمُّ ؛ خرجَ عَن تعريف الأدواتِ الكلمات الوجوديَّةُ، الأفعالُ النَّاقصةُ لاستقلالها بحسب الدَّلالةِ التَّضمنيَّة؛ لأنَّ مدلولَها التَّضمنيَّ الزَّمانُ إجمالاً وتبعاً، والمدرك كذلك غير صالح.
The particle: its meaning is present in it, but it is not understood without mentioning the related thing. And it was said: the meaning of the particle is present in both the particle and the related thing, so it is not conceptualized except by the combination of the two. It was restricted to itself alone because the particle is used for predication with something else, e.g., 'Zayd is in the house.' If you say: the verb cannot be used alone for predication, but only with its agent; I say: this is the school of the grammarians, because they consider expressions, so a pronoun must be in the predicate if it is a verb, referring back to the subject, for the sake of linking the speech, or what stands in place of the pronoun. As for the logicians, the predicate with them is the verb itself, because they attend only to meanings, and what is affirmed for the subject is the meaning of the verb. Reflect. If you say: what is the point of the commentator's saying 'it is independent in predication by itself alone' and he did not say 'about it'? I say: because the author made the individual word a division of what one predicates with, not what one predicates about. Al-‘Attar: The tools are either non-temporal or temporal, which are the defective verbs. The utmost in this matter is that their terminology does not agree with the terminology of the grammarians, and that is not necessary. End quote. This speech will have a sequel. Then, independence is a real attribute of meaning, and its meaning is that it is observed as intended essentially, not as a follower of another thing, such that it becomes a mirror for observing something else like tools. And by the dependence of the independence of meaning, predication with the word becomes valid. So the meaning of the commentator's saying 'it is independent in predication by itself alone' is that its meaning is independent due to the suitability of its expression for predication by itself alone. But this causality in knowledge means we know that its meaning is independent because we find it used in predication; that does not cause independence, rather the opposite is as you heard. So the commentator's speech is based on leniency. Hence the direction of the glossator's saying becomes clear: independence in reality is the independence of meaning in conceptuality, and predication with it is necessary for that. So the most apparent is to say in explaining the speech: it is independent in indication because its meaning is independent. Then with indication by its form. He said: 'then with indication' i.e., due to the convention, otherwise the performatives detached from time, like 'I sold' and 'I bought', would be excluded. He said: 'then with indication by its form' — the imperfect verb is objected against it, for it does not indicate one of them; rather it indicates present and future. Al-‘Attar: It is observation [such that it is] not observed as a follower of another, so that it cannot be observed without it. End quote. End quote. And the fall of what was said: that it comes with predication to depict independence, and that the commentator carried independence to what pertains to the expression; for it is accommodation with the commentator in his leniency. What supports what we mentioned is the saying of Mir Zahid: the criterion of judgment is observation and attention essentially. So since nouns and verbs are observed essentially, and the tool is observed accidentally, judgment was valid for them and not valid for it. End quote. He said: 'then with indication' if by it is meant the conjunctive implication and the conjunctive implicatum, verbs are excluded because their conjunctive implicatum is not independent due to the relation to the agent being taken as part of the conjunctive implicatum, and it is not independent, and the compound of independent and non-independent is non-independent. And if what is more general is meant, the existential verbs, the defective verbs, are excluded from the definition of tools because of their independence in terms of implicative indication, for their implicative implicatum is time, although they are tools according to the logicians. Rather, all tools are excluded because of their independence in terms of obligatory indication, for their obligatory implicatum is independent, and it is the total related thing in observation, like absolute beginning in the meaning of 'min' and the like. The answer: we choose the second branch and deny the independence of the tool in implicative and obligatory indication, based on the fact that what is meant by the independence of indication and the implicatum in observation is the suitability of the implicatum according to this indication to be used in predication, i.e., as a predicative. And time in existential verbs and the total related thing which the tools indicate are not suitable for that when they indicate them, because existential verbs indicate time inasmuch as it is a container of the relation, and the container inasmuch as it is a container is not suitable to be a predicative. Likewise, the total related thing: the tools indicate it only from the perspective that it is perceived summarily and dependently, and what is so perceived is not suitable.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) of a commentary on the definition of independence (istiqlāl) in the context of parts of speech. The author, likely al-Dasūqī, engages with earlier commentators to clarify the precise meaning of istiqlāl and its application to particles (ḥurūf), verbs (afʿāl), and nouns (asmāʾ).

The discussion begins by noting that a particle's meaning is present in itself but cannot be understood without its related term (e.g., 'in' requires a location). It is said that the particle's meaning is present in both the particle and its related term; thus, it is only fully conceptualized by the combination. The particle is restricted to itself because it is used in predication together with something else, e.g., 'Zayd is in the house.'

An objection arises: a verb also cannot be used alone in predication; it requires an agent. The reply distinguishes the grammarians' view from the logicians' view. Grammarians focus on expressions and require a pronoun linking the verb to the subject. Logicians focus on meanings; for them, the predicate is the verb itself, because the verb's meaning (the event) is what is affirmed of the subject. The author then explains why the commentator said 'it is independent in predication by itself alone' rather than 'about itself'—because the author divides the single word into what one predicates with (i.e., the predicate term) not what one predicates about (the subject).

Al-ʿAṭṭār adds that tools (adawāt) are either non-temporal or temporal (defective verbs). He notes that logicians' terminology differs from grammarians', and that is acceptable. The key point follows: independence is a real attribute of meaning—it means the meaning is observed as intended essentially, not as a follower of another thing (like a mirror for another). Based on this, predication with the word becomes valid. The commentator's statement 'it is independent in predication by itself alone' is interpreted leniently: the independence of meaning is the cause; our knowledge of that independence comes from observing its use in predication, but that observation does not create independence—it's the reverse. Thus, the glossator (muḥashshī) is correct: true independence is conceptual self-sufficiency of meaning, and predication is a necessary consequence.

The passage then discusses the phrase 'with indication by its form.' Al-Dasūqī explains that 'with indication' refers to conventional meaning; otherwise, performative verbs like 'I sold' would be excluded. He raises an objection about the imperfect verb, which does not indicate a single time but rather present and future. Al-ʿAṭṭār reinforces the definition of independence as observation without dependence on another.

Mir Zāhid's statement is cited to support the view: the criterion is essential observation. Nouns and verbs are observed essentially; tools are observed accidentally. Therefore, judgment (independence) applies to the former, not the latter.

Finally, a detailed analysis is given of the phrase 'with indication' considering different types of signification (conjunctive, implicative, obligatory). If conjunctive signification is meant, verbs are excluded because their conjunctive meaning includes the relation to the agent, which is non-independent. If broader signification is meant, existential and defective verbs would be excluded from the definition of tools because they independently indicate time via implicative signification, though logicians classify them as tools. Moreover, all tools would be excluded via obligatory signification because they obligatorily imply an independent implicatum (e.g., 'min' implies 'beginning'). The solution: we choose the broader interpretation but deny the independence of tools in implicative and obligatory signification, because the intended independence is suitability for predication (being a predicative). Time as a container and the total related thing as a secondary perception are not suitable to be predicatives. Hence, tools remain non-independent.

Key Terms
الاستقلال (al-istiqlāl): Conceptual self-sufficiency: a meaning is observed and intended essentially, not as a follower of another thing. Predication follows from this independence, not vice versa. [Note: No significant shift—this term is stable across the tradition, though some later texts emphasize the mental observation aspect.]
الحرف (al-ḥarf): Particle (tool word) whose meaning is present but only understood with its related term; it is not independent in predication. [Note: In logic, al-ḥarf includes particles and sometimes defective verbs; grammarians restrict it to non-verb particles.]
الفعل (al-fiʿl): Verb: for logicians, the predicate itself (the meaning of the event), independent in meaning; for grammarians, it needs a pronoun to connect to the subject. [Note: The logician's definition of fiʿl differs from the grammarian's; the passage clarifies this distinction.]
الإخبار (al-ikhbār): Predication: asserting something of something; it is valid only if the meaning of the predicate is independent. [Note: In logic, ikhbār is about the meaning; in grammar, it involves explicit linguistic linkage.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the real meaning of 'istiqlāl' (independence) of a word's meaning?
A) The word can be used in predication by itself without any other word.
B) The meaning is conceptually self-sufficient, observed essentially and not as a follower of another.
C) The word is a noun, not a verb or particle.
D) The word indicates time, like defective verbs.

Key Takeaway
Independence (istiqlal) is conceptual self-sufficiency of meaning; predication is a consequence, not the definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify each of the following Arabic words as independent or dependent according to the refined definition of istiqlal: 'زيد' (Zayd), 'في' (in), 'يكتب' (writes). Justify each answer by referring to whether the meaning is observed essentially or as a follower.

Distinguishing Logical Kalima from Grammatical Verb
Definition of kalima in logic vs grammar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the logical definition of kalima from the grammatical definition and identify which words qualify as kalima according to logicians.

Core Idea
In logic, kalima is defined by its form indicating time, not by its grammatical category.

The distinction between logical and grammatical definitions is crucial for precise reasoning. In logic, a word's classification depends on its semantic function, not its grammatical label. This passage clarifies what counts as a 'kalima' (verb) in logic, resolving apparent contradictions with grammar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining condition of kalima in logic
Look for the phrase 'صيغته على أحد الأزمنة الثلاثة' (its form upon one of the three times). This is the core condition: a kalima must have a form (sighah) that indicates one of the three times (past, present, future).
2
Contrast with the grammatical definition
The text says 'وعند النحاة : فعل' (according to grammarians: a verb). Grammarians consider aktionsart and other features, but logicians focus solely on time indication.
3
Examine the problem of the present tense (mudari‘)
The present tense indicates both present and future, but by original coinage it indicates only one of them. The answer explains that 'ma‘a al-dalalah' means indication by original coinage, and the present tense ambiguously indicates both. This answer includes performative verbs like ni‘ma, bi’sa, ‘asa, and laysa, which are detached from time but still have verb forms.
Performative verbs are included because their form resembles verbs, even though they do not indicate time.
4
Extend to nouns of action (ism fi‘l)
The commentary explains that nouns of action are included because their indication of time is general, whether mediated or not. So even words like 'صه' (hush!) may be considered kalima if their form indicates time in a broad sense.
This shows the logical definition is broader than the grammatical one.

Chapter: On Investigations of Expressions ... and its form upon one of the three times is a word (kalima), and according to grammarians: a verb (fi‘l). And it was answered: that his statement 'So with indication' means by original coinage, and the present tense by original coinage only indicates one of them because it was coined for the present and future by coinage, and by this answer the performative verbs that are detached from time enter into 'word' like ni‘ma, bi’sa, ‘asa, and laysa. (His statement: 'and its form') is an explanatory conjunction; i.e., its form that occurs to the letters due to movement and quiescence, and the precedence of some letters over others, and the delayed sequence of some letters from others. Qutb al-Din al-Razi said: The intended meaning of 'hay'ah' and 'sighah' is the form that occurs to the letters in consideration of their precedence and delay, their movements and quiescences, and it is the image of the word. Commentary
This passage defines the logical term 'kalima' and distinguishes it from the grammatical term 'fi‘l'. The matn states that a word's form indicating one of the three times qualifies it as 'kalima' in logic, while grammarians call it 'fi‘l'. A key problem arises: the present tense (mudari‘) indicates both present and future, but by original coinage (asl al-wad‘) it indicates both only if considered separately? The answer explains that the phrase 'ma‘a al-dalalah' means indication by original coinage, and the present tense by original coinage indicates one of them (either present or future) because it was coined for both, but the indication is ambiguous. This allows the inclusion of performative verbs (af‘al insha'iyyah) like ni‘ma, bi’sa, ‘asa, and laysa, which are detached from time but still considered 'kalima' because their form indicates time in some way? Actually, the text says these are included by the answer; they are detached from time yet still count as kalima because they have the form of verbs. The commentary then explains 'wa sighatihi' as an explanatory conjunction, referring to the form produced by letter order, movements, and pauses. Qutb al-Din al-Razi clarifies that 'hay'ah' and 'sighah' refer to this form, which is the image of the word. Finally, 'ism fi‘l' (nouns of action) are included because their indication of time through form is general, whether mediated or not, as stated in Sharh al-Matali‘.

Condition of Material in the Definition of Kalima
Author explains the condition that the form must be in a conventional, inflectable material.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given Arabic word meets the condition of being in a conventional, inflectable material that indicates time by its form.

Core Idea
A word's form must be built from a real, inflectable Arabic root to indicate time.

The author refines the definition of 'kalima' by adding a condition: the form must be in a conventional material (maddah mawdu‘ah) that is inflectable (mutasarrif). This excludes nonsense words like 'jasq' and nouns like 'hajar' that happen to have verb forms but lack time indication. The passage also addresses whether this condition applies only to Arabic, concluding that since the science is compiled in Arabic, it is acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main condition
Notice that the author says 'bi-hay'atihi' (by its form) with the preposition 'bi' to indicate a condition: the form must be in a material that is conventionally coined (mawdu‘ah) and inflectable (mutasarrif). The word 'jasq' and 'hajar' are rejected because they lack these properties.
2
Understand why the preposition 'bi' is used
The author uses 'bi-hay'atihi' instead of 'hay'ah' to stress that the form is a condition. Without 'bi', it would just mean 'a form', not a required condition.
3
Distinguish between form of root letters and extra letters
The intended form is that of the root letters (huruf usul), not the extra letters. Example: 'ta‘allam' (command) and 'ta‘allama' (past) share the same root form despite different time references due to extra letters.
4
Recognize that time indication is by coinage (wad‘)
The indication of time is built into the word by linguistic convention. Words like 'ni‘ma' (perfect of praise) are detached from time and thus excluded from being a 'kalima' in this sense.
5
Examine the cross-linguistic objection and response
The author states that time indication by form is only valid in Arabic, giving Persian examples 'amad' and 'ayad'. Al-Sayyid responds that the art of logic is universal but the reliance on Arabic is justified because the science is mostly compiled in Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(His statement: 'by its form and pattern') means: on condition that it is in a conventional [coined] material that is inflectable, so that [objections] like jasq and hajar are not raised, for they are upon the form of daraba with no indication of time. And to alert to that, he said 'by its form' and did not say 'a form'. Then the conjunction of 'pattern' to 'form' is for explanation, due to their fame in the intended meaning. And what is meant by it is the form that occurs to the root letters in consideration of their precedence and delay, their movements and quiescences, not upon the other [non-root letters] because no attention is given to what occurs to the other; such that it makes ta‘allam (command) and ta‘allama (past) upon one form. Then the intended indication is according to coinage, so that the verbs detached from time are excluded. The author said: The indication of the word of time by the pattern is only valid in the Arabic language, not in the language of the non-Arabs, because your saying 'amad' and 'ayad' are unified in pattern but different in time, even though the consideration of this art regarding expressions is universal, not specific to one language over another. Commentary
This passage expands on the definition of 'kalima' by specifying the condition that the form (hay'ah/sighah) must be in a conventional (mawdu‘ah) and inflectable (mutasarrif) material. This excludes nonsense words like 'jasq' and 'hajar' which happen to have the same form as 'daraba' but do not indicate time. The intended form is that of the root letters (huruf usul), not the additions, because for example the command 'ta‘allam' (learn!) and the past 'ta‘allama' (he learned) have the same form but different time indications? Actually, they differ in vowels but the form is similar. The indication of time is by coinage (wad‘) to exclude performative verbs (like ni‘ma) which are detached from time. Then the author states that such indication by pattern is valid only in Arabic, not in non-Arabic languages, giving the Persian example 'amad' (he came) and 'ayad' (he comes) which have the same form but differ in time. Al-Sayyid responds that the art (mantiq) generally deals with expressions universally, but due to greater concern with Arabic (in which the science is usually compiled), it is acceptable to specify this condition for Arabic.

Definition of Kalima and Its Three Conditions
Author defines kalima and specifies three conditions excluding particles and nouns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conditions that define a kalima (verb) and apply them to distinguish verbs from nouns and particles in Arabic.

Core Idea
A verb is defined by three conditions: independent meaning, temporal indication, and morphological form.

In Islamic logic, the term kalima has a specific technical meaning narrower than its grammatical use. Al-Tadhheeb defines kalima as a word that independently conveys meaning while indicating one of the three times through its morphological pattern. This lesson unpacks the three conditions and shows how they exclude particles, non-temporal nouns, and temporal nouns that lack verbal form.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of kalima in the passage.
Find where the author defines kalima as a predicate of a deleted subject, and note the three conditions that follow.
The key phrase is 'فَبِقَيدِ الاستقلال...'.
2
Understand the condition of independence (istiqlal).
The word must be independently meaningful without relying on other words. This excludes particles like 'hal' and 'lam'.
3
Understand the condition of temporal indication.
The word must indicate one of the three times (past, present, future). This excludes nouns that have no time reference, like 'Zaid'.
Proper names and many common nouns fall under this exclusion.
4
Understand the condition of indication by form (hay'a).
The temporal meaning must come from the morphological pattern, not the lexical root. This excludes words like 'zaman' (time) and 'ams' (yesterday) that indicate time but not by a verbal pattern.
These nouns indicate time through their substance (madda), not through a verb form.
5
Apply the three conditions to classify examples.
Test words like 'daraba' (he hit): it meets all three conditions (independent, past tense, verb pattern). Compare with 'amsi': meets independence and temporal indication but fails the form condition.
Practice with other verbs, nouns, and particles from Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مباحث الألفاظ
وقوله : (كلمةٌ) خبر مبتدأ محذوف، والتَّقديرُ : فهو حال كونه معَ الدَّلالةِ على أحدِها كلمةٌ .
فَبِقَيدِ الاستقلال تخرج الأداة، وبقيدِ الدَّلالة على أحدِ الأزمنةِ الثَّلاثةِ يخرج الاسمُ الَّذي لا يدلُّ على الزَّمانِ أصلاً .
وبقيدِ الهيئة والصيغة يخرج الاسم الذي يدلُّ على الزَّمانِ، لكن لا بهيئته وصيغته، بل بحسب جَوهَرِه ومادَّتِه، كالزَّمانِ، والأمسِ،
قوله : (فبقيد الاستقلال تخرج الأداة) أي: لأنها غير مستقلة بالمفهومية؛ لتوقف فهم معناها على الغير؛ وهو المتعلق.
قوله : (يخرج الاسم الذي لا يدل على الزمان أصلاً) أي: كـ: زيد وعمرو.
A Section: On the investigation of words. And His saying: (kalima) is a predicate of an omitted subject, and the estimation is: so it is in the state of being with indication of one of them a kalima. By the condition of independence, the particle is excluded, and by the condition of indication of one of the three times, the noun that does not indicate time at all is excluded. And by the condition of the form and pattern, the noun that indicates time, but not by its form and pattern, rather according to its substance and matter, like 'zaman' and 'ams', is excluded. His saying: (by the condition of independence, the particle is excluded) meaning: because it is not independent in conceptuality, due to the understanding of its meaning being dependent on something else, which is the related. His saying: (the noun that does not indicate time at all is excluded) meaning: like Zaid and Amr.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'kalima' (word/verb) and explains three conditional exclusions. The author begins by parsing the grammatical structure, then enumerates three conditions that distinguish kalima from other parts of speech. The first condition is independence (istiqlal): kalima must be independently meaningful, which excludes particles (adawat) whose meaning depends on other words. The second condition is indication of one of the three times (past, present, future): this excludes nouns that do not indicate time at all, like proper names (Zaid, Amr). The third condition is indication by form (hay'a) and pattern (sigha): this excludes nouns that indicate time but not through their morphological pattern, but rather through their lexical substance (jawhar/madda). Examples given are 'zaman' (time) and 'ams' (yesterday), which indicate time by their substance, not by a specific verbal pattern. The commentary adds that particles are excluded because their meaning is not self-sufficient, and nouns like Zaid and Amr are excluded because they carry no temporal reference.

Key Takeaway
The definition of kalima in Islamic logic is a controlled term: it must be independent, indicate time, and do so through its morphological pattern.

The Three Modes of Tashkīk: Priority, Preferability, and Intensity
Commentator discusses the types of gradation (tashkīk) and debate over shiddah as a separate kind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between awwaliyyah, awlawiyyah, and shiddah as modes of tashkīk and evaluate the debate regarding shiddah as a separate mode using Mir Zahid's reclassification.

Core Idea
Shiddah qualifies the individual, not the universal; Mir Zahid reclassifies tashkīk into three types based on what is qualified.

Tashkīk (gradation) is a key concept in Islamic logic, describing how a term applies to different individuals with varying degrees. In this passage, the commentator explains the standard three modes—awwaliyyah (priority), awlawiyyah (preferability), and shiddah (intensity)—and presents a debate about whether shiddah is a distinct mode or reducible to awlawiyyah. Understanding this classification helps you analyze definitions and arguments in kalam and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three standard modes of tashkīk
From the passage, list awwaliyyah (essential priority), awlawiyyah (mental preferability), and shiddah (abundance of effects). Note the example: existence in the Necessary (awwalī) vs. possible; whiteness in snow vs. ivory (shiddah).
The passage mentions a fourth mode (increase and decrease) but it is not widely accepted.
2
Understand the objection raised by al-Jalal
Al-Jalal argues that since awwaliyyah and awlawiyyah are distinct despite awwaliyyah including awlawiyyah, shiddah should also be distinct. This challenges the author of the matn, who only treated the first two.
3
Analyze Mir Zahid's reclassification
Mir Zahid proposes a principled division: tashkīk modes are determined by what they qualify. Shiddah qualifies the individual only (e.g., more intense blackness), awwaliyyah qualifies the universal only (priority of existence), and awlawiyyah qualifies both (preferability). This resolves the debate by showing shiddah is not a separate mode but a cause of preferability.
The commentator corrects a misunderstanding that awwaliyyah does not reduce to awlawiyyah.
4
Apply the classification to an example
Consider the statement: 'Existence in the Necessary is prior to existence in the possible.' Using Mir Zahid's classification, this is awwaliyyah because it qualifies the predication (the concept of existence) itself, not an individual instance.
The commentator clarifies that awwaliyyah is essential precedence, not temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظِ
وذلك التفاوتُ إِمَّا بِأَوَّلِيَّةٍ) كالوجودِ،
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : وَذَلِكَ) أي : التَّفاوت المصوّر بكون حصولِ المعنى في بعض الأفرادِ أولى مِن حصولِهِ في بعض (قَوْلُهُ : بأَوَّلِيَّةٍ) الباء سببيَّة .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : إِمَّا بِأَوَّلِيَّةٍ أَوْ أَوْلَوِيَّةٍ قالَ الجَلالُ : لا يُقَالُ الثَّانية تشتمل على الأُوْلَى أيضاً ؛ فإنَّ اتّصافَ العِلَّةِ بِالوجودِ أَوْلَى مِنَ اتِّصافِ المعلولِ بِهِ؛ إذْ لَا يَخفى أنَّ اعتبار الأوَّليَّةِ غيرُ اعتبار الأولويَّةِ وإنْ كانَ الأقدمُ أولى، لكن ينقدحُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ أَنَّ الأشدّيَّةَ أيضاً كذلك، فَلْتُجْعَلْ قِسْمَاً آخَرَ .ا.هـ. يعني: أنَّ المشهور في التَّشكيكِ اعتبارُ التّفاوتِ بأحد الوجوه الثَّلاثَةِ وَهِيَ الأولويَّةُ بمعنى التَّقدُّم بالذَّاتِ؛ أعني : العليَّةَ، والأولويَّةُ بمعنى الأنسبيَّةِ في نظر العقل، والأشدّيَّةُ بمعنى أكثرِيَّةِ الآثارِ كَمَا في الأبيض بالنسبة إلى الثَّلْجِ والعَاجِ ، وبَقِيَ قِسم رابع ذكرَهُ الجَلالُ في حاشية التجريدِ وهو الزيادة والنقصان، لكنَّه غيرُ شَهير، والمصنِّفُ اكتفى بالأَوَّلَيْنِ؛ لأنَّ الثَّالِثَ يَستلزمُ الثَّاني؛ فَاتَّجَهَ عليهِ أَنَّهُ لَمَّا جعلَ الأَوَّليَّةَ قِسْماً بِرَأْسِهِ مُقَابِلا لِلأولويَّةِ مَعَ كَوْنِ الأوليةِ مُسْتَمِلَةٌ عليها لأجل أنَّ اعتبار الأوَّليَّةِ غير اعتبارِ الأولويَّةِ، أَنَّ اعتبار الأشديَّةِ غيرُ اعتبار الأولويّةِ، فَلْتُجْعَلْ قِسْماً آخَرَ مُقابلاً لهما لأجل هذا الاعتبار، وأجابَ مير زاهد بأنَّ التَّشكيكَ على وجوه ثلاثة ؛ الأَوَّل : مَا يَتَصفُ الفردُ فقط وَلَا يَتَّصِفُ بِهِ صِدْقُ الكُلّيّ عليه كالأشدّيَّةِ والثَّاني : مَا يَتَصفُ بِهِ الصِّدقُ فقط وَهُوَ الأَوَّليَّةُ ، والثَّالث : مَا يَتَصفُ بِهِ الفردُ والصَّدقُ معاً والأولويَّةُ مِن هذا القبيل، والمصنِّفُ لم يجعَلِ الأَوَّلَ مِن وجوه التّشكيكِ؛ لأَنَّ مَا يَتَّصِفُ بِهِ الفردُ وَلَا يتَّصِفُ بِهِ الصِّدقُ ليسَ في الحقيقةِ مِن وجوه التّشكيكِ؛ بَلْ مِن مُوجِباتِ الأولويَّةِ التي هي من وجوهه ا.هـ. وما في المحشي من عدم ظهورِ رِجوعِ الأَوَّليَّةِ لِلأولوية وأنَّ الأمرَ بِالعَكْسِ ؛ وَهم، إذ حيثُ كان الوجود في الواجب أتم وأولى منه في الممكن ؛ لِكَوْنِهِ واجباً أي: لا يسبقه ولا يلحقهُ عَدَم؛ كان سابقاً في نظر العقل وسابقاً أيضاً سبقاً ذاتياً في الخارج على وجودِ الممكن، وهذا معنى الأوَّليَّة إذ المراد بها السَّبِقُ الذَّاتِيُّ كَمَا نَبَّهُوا عَليهِ؛ لَا الزَّمانيُّ؛ تدبَّر، وبقي هَهُنا بحث وهو
فإِنَّه في الواجب قبل حصوله في الممكن .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : أَوْ أَوْلَوِيَّةٍ) أي : خاصَّة بمعنى الأتمّيَّة والأكملية، بخلاف الأولوية
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : أَوْ أَوْلَوِيَّةٍ) أي : خاصَّة بمعنى الأتمّيَّة والأكملية، بخلاف الأولوية
نَّهم فسَّرُوا الأشدّيَّةَ بأكثريَّةِ آثارِ الكُلّيّ في بعض الأفراد، ولا يَخفَى أَنَّهُ يَستلزمُ التَّشكيك فى الذَّاتِيَّاتِ كَالإنسان، وأشارَ الجَلالُ في حاشية التَّجريدِ إلى جوابِهِ؛ بأن معنى كَوْنِ أَحدِ الفردَيْنِ أشدَّ كونه بحيثُ يَنتزعُ منه العقلُ بمعونة الوهم أمثال الأضعف، ويحلّلهُ إليها بِضربٍ مِنَ التَّحليل، فَمَفهومُ الأَسْوَدِ مَقولٌ بالتَّسْكِيكِ على أسودَيْنِ مُعيَّنَيْنِ؛ باعتبار أنَّ السَّوادَ في أحدِهما أَزْيَدُ مِنَ الآخَرِ، بمعنى أنَّ العقل بمعونة الوهم ينتزعُ مِن أحدهما أمثالَ الآخَرِ، وفي شرحِ سُلَّم العلوم؛ قالَ الإشراقيُونَ : الزِّيادةُ والقُوَّةُ والسِّدَّةُ أمرٌ واحد وهو كمالُ الماهية، لكن إذا وُجِدَتْ في الكمّ سُمِّيَتْ زيادةً، وإذا وُجِدَتْ في الجوهرِ سُمِّيَتْ قُوَّةً، وإذا وُجِدَتْ في الكَيْفِ سُمِّيَتْ شِدَّةٌ، وَكَذا أضدادُهَا، لكنَّ هذهِ إطلاقات عرفيَّةٌ لا اعتدادَ بِهَا في العلوم الحُكميَّةِ، والمشّاؤونَ قالُوا بتغايرها؛ نظراً إلى الإطلاقات، وناقضُوا أنفسَهُم؛ حيثُ لم يُجوِّزُوا كونَ الخطِّ أشدَّ خَطَّيَّةً، وجوَّزُوا أَشَدَّ طُولاً، مَعَ أَنَّ الطُّول هو الخَطُّ، ثم قال: واختلفُوا هَل الجوهرُ يشتد أم لا؟ قالَ الإشراقيُّونَ: نَعَمْ، وهو ظاهر، فإنَّهم عَنَوا بها كمال الماهيَّة، والماهيَّةُ الجوهريَّةُ في الفيل أكمل مِنَ البعوضة؛ لظهورِ آثارِ الكثرة في الفيل دونَهَا، وعلى مَا فَسَّرَهُ أَتباعُ المُشَّائِيْنَ لهُ تجويز أيضاً، فإِنَّ مِنَ الجائز أنْ يكونَ بعضُ المفارقات؛ بحيثُ ينتزع عنه أمثالُ مفارقَ أُخَر، ولم يدلَّ دليل على خلافه، وقد ادَّعَى الإشراقيون فيه المشاهدة بالرياضات، وقال المشَّاؤُونَ: لا يشتد الجوهر، ولم يقيموا عليه دليلاً؛ بل بنوا على مجرى العرف؛ حيثُ لم يُطلَق على جوهرٍ أنَّهُ أشد من جوهرٍ آخَرَ، والزِّيادة والنُّقصانُ على أصلهم أيضاً يتّصفُ الجوهرُ بِهِمَا، فإنَّهم قالُوا: المقدارُ جوهر، وهو غيرُ الجسم مع (قَوْلُهُ: فَإِنَّهُ فِي الْوَاجِبِ قَبْلَ حُصُوْلِهِ فِي الْمُمْكِن) أي: إِنَّ الوجود الواجبيَّ سابق على الوجودِ الممكنيَّ سَبقاً ذاتيا؛ لأنَّ الثَّاني أثرُ ناشى عَن الأَوَّلِ .
A chapter on the discourses of words. And that variation is either by priority (awwaliyyah), like existence. (His statement: 'And that') i.e., the variation depicted by the occurrence of the meaning in some individuals being more appropriate than its occurrence in others. (His statement: 'by priority') the ba' is causal. (His statement: 'either by priority or preferability') Al-Jalal said: It cannot be said that the second includes the first as well; for the attribute of the cause by existence is more appropriate than the attribute of the effect by it, since it is not hidden that the consideration of priority is different from the consideration of preferability, even if the prior is more appropriate, but it follows from that that intensity (shiddah) is also likewise, so let it be made another division. End quote. Meaning: The well-known in tashkik is considering variation in one of three ways: priority in the sense of precedence in essence, i.e., causality; preferability in the sense of suitability in the view of the intellect; and intensity in the sense of more effects, like in whiteness with respect to snow and ivory. And there remained a fourth division mentioned by al-Jalal in his gloss on al-Tajrid, namely increase and decrease, but it is not well-known. And the author sufficed with the first two because the third entails the second. So it was objected to him that when he made priority a separate division opposed to preferability, despite the fact that priority includes it, because the consideration of priority is different from the consideration of preferability, then the consideration of intensity is also different from the consideration of preferability, so let it be made another division opposed to them for this consideration. Mir Zahid answered that tashkik is of three types: first, what qualified the individual only and does not qualify the universal predication of it, like intensity; second, what qualifies the predication only, and that is priority; third, what qualifies both the individual and the predication, and preferability is of this type. And the author did not make the first a type of tashkik because what qualifies the individual and does not qualify the predication is not in reality a type of tashkik, but rather a cause of preferability which is one of its types. End quote. And what is in the gloss from the lack of appearance of the return of priority to preferability and that the matter is the opposite is a mistake, for where existence in the Necessary is more perfect and more appropriate than in the possible, because it is necessary, i.e., no non-existence precedes it or follows it, it is prior in the view of the intellect and also prior by essential precedence in the external world over the existence of the possible, and this is the meaning of priority, for what is meant by it is essential precedence, as they pointed out, not temporal. Reflect. And there remains here a research, and it is that it is in the Necessary before its occurrence in the possible. (His statement: 'or preferability') i.e., specifically in the sense of perfection and completeness, contrary to priority. (His statement: 'or preferability') i.e., specifically in the sense of perfection and completeness, contrary to priority. They interpreted intensity as the abundance of the effects of the universal in some individuals, and it is not hidden that this entails tashkik in the essentials like 'human'. And al-Jalal indicated in his gloss on al-Tajrid an answer to it: that the meaning of one of the two individuals being more intense is that it is such that the intellect with the help of the imagination extracts from it the likes of the weaker and analyzes it into them by a kind of analysis. So the concept of 'black' is said with tashkik of two specific blacks, considering that the blackness in one of them is more than the other, in the sense that the intellect with the help of the imagination extracts from one the likes of the other. And in the commentary on Sullam al-'Ulum: The Ishraqis said: increase, power, and intensity are one thing, which is the perfection of the essence, but if found in quantity it is called increase, if found in substance it is called power, if found in quality it is called intensity, and likewise their opposites. But these are conventional usages not considered in the philosophical sciences. The Peripatetics said they are distinct, looking at the usages, and they contradicted themselves where they did not allow a line to be more intense in 'line-ness', but allowed more intense in length, although length is the line. Then he said: They disagreed: does substance admit intensity? The Ishraqis said yes, and it is obvious, for they meant by it the perfection of the essence, and the substantial essence in the elephant is more perfect than in the mosquito, due to the appearance of many effects in the elephant unlike it. And according to what the followers of the Peripatetics interpreted, there is also allowance, for it is possible that some immaterial entities are such that the intellect extracts from them the likes of other immaterial entities, and no proof indicates the contrary. The Ishraqis claimed in it observation through spiritual exercises. The Peripatetics said substance does not become intense, and they did not provide a proof for it, but rather based it on conventional usage, since it is not said of a substance that it is more intense than another substance. And increase and decrease according to their principle also qualify substance, for they said that quantity is a substance, and it is other than body, with (His statement: 'for it is in the Necessary before its occurrence in the possible') i.e., the existence of the Necessary is prior to the existence of the possible with essential precedence, because the second is an effect arising from the first.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary (hāshiyah) on a section about the discourses of words (mabāhith al-alfāẓ), specifically focusing on the concept of gradation (tashkīk) and its subdivisions. The commentator, likely al-Dasūqī or al-ʿAṭṭār, explains and refines the classification of variation (tafāwut) in terms of priority (awwaliyyah), preferability (awlawiyyah), and intensity (shiddah). The passage opens by stating that variation in the occurrence of a meaning across individuals is either by priority or preferability, using existence as an example. Then it delves into a debate: al-Jalāl (al-Dawānī) argues that intensity should be a third type because its consideration is distinct from preferability, just as priority is distinct. The commentator explains the standard threefold division: priority (essential precedence), preferability (mental suitability), and intensity (abundance of effects). A fourth type, increase and decrease, is mentioned but not widely accepted. The author of the matn (the main text) only used the first two because intensity entails preferability, but an objection is raised: if priority is separate despite including preferability, then intensity should also be separate. Mīrzā Zāhid resolves this by reclassifying tashkīk into three types based on what qualifies: the individual alone (intensity), the universal alone (priority), or both (preferability). He argues intensity is not a true mode of tashkīk but a cause of preferability. The commentator then corrects a mistaken notion that priority does not return to preferability, explaining that priority in the Necessary as essential precedence also aligns with mental precedence. The passage then moves to the nature of intensity, quoting from Sharḥ Sullam al-ʿUlūm about the Ishraqi and Peripatetic views. The Ishraqis see increase, power, and intensity as one thing—perfection of essence—differing only by subject (quantity, substance, quality). The Peripatetics distinguish them but contradict themselves, as they allow intensity in length but not in line. The debate extends to whether substance admits intensity: Ishraqis affirm it based on perfection (elephant vs. mosquito), while Peripatetics deny it based on common usage, though they inconsistently accept increase/decrease in substance (quantity as substance). The passage concludes with a gloss affirming that the Necessary's existence is essentially prior to the possible's, as the latter is an effect.

Checkpoint
According to Mir Zahid's classification in the passage, what does awwaliyyah (priority) qualify?
A) The individual alone
B) The universal alone (the predication)
C) Both the individual and the universal
D) Neither the individual nor the universal

Key Takeaway
Tashkīk has three standard modes: awwaliyyah (essential priority), awlawiyyah (mental preferability), and shiddah (abundance of effects), with Mir Zahid reclassifying them based on what is qualified—individual, universal, or both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Using Mir Zahid's classification, determine which mode of tashkīk applies when we say 'snow is whiter than ivory'. Identify whether intensity qualifies the individual, the universal, or both. Explain based on the passage.
?
Task 2: Consider the statement 'The Necessary's existence is prior to the possible's existence.' Which mode does this exemplify? Justify your answer by referencing the definitions of awwaliyyah, awlawiyyah, and shiddah from the passage.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
8 min
Understanding the Ambiguous Term (Mushakkik): Definition, Objection, and Defense
New chapter defines the ambiguous term (mushakkik) and contrasts it with univocal (mutawati) and equivocal (mushtarak).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defining characteristic of a mushakkik term, distinguish it from mutawati and mushtarak, and explain al-Qarafi's argument for its validity.

Core Idea
Mushakkik is a distinct category: shared meaning, but graded perfection.

In this passage, the author introduces a third category of terms: mushakkik (ambiguous), which lies between univocal (mutawati) and equivocal (mushtarak). He illustrates it with the example of existence (wujud), which is predicated of God more intensely than of creatures. The passage then records an objection by Ibn al-Tilimsani questioning whether mushakkik is a real category, and al-Qarafi's famous response that secures its place in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three term categories
Locate the mention of mutawati (univocal) and mushtarak (equivocal) in the text. Note how mushakkik is distinguished from both: it shares a core meaning like mutawati, but with gradation.
The text explicitly compares mushakkik to the other two.
2
Extract the definition of mushakkik
Find the definition: a term whose individuals agree in the core meaning but differ in priority, intensity, or perfection. The name 'mushakkik' comes from the doubt it causes.
The root 'shakk' (doubt) is key.
3
Examine the examples
Look at the examples: existence (wujud) in God vs. creatures, whiteness in snow vs. ivory, light in the sun vs. moon. Notice how the difference is one of degree, not kind.
Al-Qarafi argues that the difference is from the same genus as the named.
4
Analyze Ibn al-Tilimsani's objection
Ibn al-Tilimsani claims that if the difference in meaning enters the definition, the term is equivocal (mushtarak); if not, it is univocal (mutawati). Therefore, mushakkik is superfluous.
This is a logical challenge: can there be a third option?
5
Evaluate al-Qarafi's defense
Al-Qarafi responds that in mushakkik, the difference (e.g., intensity) is not part of the core meaning but is a property of the individuals that is of the same genus as the meaning itself. Thus, both mutawati and mushakkik share a common core, but mushakkik has an intrinsic gradation.
This defense establishes mushakkik as a real category in logic.

فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ بأوليَّةٍ كما مرَّ ، وإما بأولوية كالوجودِ أيضاً، فإنَّه في الواجب أتم وأولى وتسميته بالمشكّكِ؛ لأنَّ النَّاظر فيه مشكك، هل هو متواطئ من حيثُ اتِّفاقُ أفراده في أصل المعنى، الدسوقي السَّابقة في الشَّارح؛ فإنَّها أعم، فليس فيه اتحاد الشببِ والمسبب، وقوله: (أولوية)؛ أي : أو شَدَّة وضعف كما قال غيره، ومثاله الوجود، فإِنَّهُ في الواجب أشدُّ؛ أي: لا يقبلُ الزَّوال، وفي الممكن ضعيف؛ أي: يقبلُ الزَّوال، وإِنْ كَانَ مَثَلَ له بعضُهُم بِالبياض ؛ فإِنَّهُ في الثَّلْجِ أبيضَ منه في العاج، وبالنُّورِ؛ فإنَّهُ في الشَّمسِ نقلاً أشدُّ منه في القمر والسراج . اهـ ياسين (قَوْلُهُ : أَتَمُّ) أي : لِكونِهِ لا يقبلُ الانتفاء بخلافِهِ في الممكن، فَإِنَّهُ يَقْبَلُ الانتفاء . (قَوْلُهُ : وَأَوْلَى) أي: أكمل ؛ عطفُ تفسير . (قَوْلُهُ : لِأَنَّ النَّظَرَ فِيْهِ مُشكِّكٌ بكسر الكافِ؛ اسم فاعل؛ أي : لأَنَّ النَّظْرَ فِيهِ الكافِ يوقعُ النَّاظر في الشَّلِّ؛ هل هو مُتواطى أو مُشترك؟، ويصح قراءتُهُ بفتح أَنَّه اسم مفعول؛ أي: لأنَّ النَّظر فيهِ واقع عليهِ الشَّكُ، وعليهِ؛ فَالإِسنادُ على العطار (قَوْلُهُ : أَتَهُ) لِعَدَم سَبقِ العدم عليهِ وعدم لحوقِهِ، وأَوْلَى) لامتناع تصورِ انفكاكِهِ عنه؛ لأنَّهُ عينُ ذاتِهِ، فَذَاتُهُ تَعالى أحقُّ مِنَ الممكن بالوجودِ، وَهَهُنا كلام نفيس يطلب من الرِّسالةِ الزَّوراء وحواشيها للجَلال الدواني. (قَوْلُهُ : لِأَنَّ النَّاظِرَ فِيهِ مُشَكَّلٌ بصيغة اسم المفعول، وما في المتن بصيغة اسم الفاعل والإسناد فيه مجازي؛ إذْ هو محلَّ التَّشكيكِ، ومِن هَهُنا قالَ ابنُ التلمساني : لا حقيقةَ لِلمشكِّكِ ؛ لأنَّ ما حصلَ بِهِ الاختلافُ إِنْ دخل في التّسمية؛ كانَ اللَّفظُ مُشتركاً، وإن لم يدخل بل وضعَ لِلقَدْرِ المشترك؛ فهو المتواطئ وأجابَ القرافي بأنَّ كُلا من المتواطئ والمشككِ؛ موضوع لِلقَدْرِ المشترك، ولكنَّ الاختلاف إنْ كانَ بأمورٍ من جنس المسمَّى ؛ فهو المصطلح على تسميته بالمشكَّكِ،
Chapter: On Topics of Words [Existence is] with priority as previously, or with priority like existence also, for it is in the Necessary Being more perfect and more prior. And it is named ambiguous (mushakkik) because the one who reflects on it is doubtful whether it is univocal (mutawati) since its individuals agree in the core meaning. Al-Dasooqi: [The priority] earlier in the commentator is more general, so there is no unity of cause and effect. And his statement: (priority) i.e., or intensity and weakness as others said. Its example is existence, for it in the Necessary Being is more intense, i.e., does not accept cessation, and in the contingent is weak, i.e., accepts cessation. Although some gave the example of whiteness, for it in snow is whiter than in ivory, and of light, for it in the sun [according to transmission] is more intense than in the moon and lamp. End of Yasin. (His statement: more perfect) i.e., because it does not accept nonexistence unlike in the contingent, for it accepts nonexistence. (His statement: and more prior) i.e., more perfect; an explanatory conjunction. (His statement: because the reflection in it is ambiguous) with kasra on the kaf as active participle; i.e., because the reflection in it causes the reflector to be in doubt whether it is univocal or equivocal. And it is permissible to read it with fatha as passive participle; i.e., because reflection in it is subject to doubt. Thus the attribution is metaphorical. Al-Attar: (His statement: 'more perfect') due to the absence of prior nonexistence and subsequent nonexistence; and 'more prior' due to the impossibility of conceiving its separation from it, because it is identical to His essence, so His essence (exalted) is more deserving of existence than the contingent. And here there is a precious discussion to be sought from al-Risala al-Zawra and its glosses by al-Jalal al-Dawani. (His statement: because the reflector in it is dubious) with the form of passive participle, while what is in the text is with the form of active participle and the attribution is metaphorical, since it is the locus of doubt. From here Ibn al-Tilimsani said: There is no reality to the ambiguous term, because what the difference occurs in: if it enters into the naming, then the word is equivocal; and if it does not enter but is placed for the common core, then it is univocal. Al-Qarafi replied: Both the univocal and the ambiguous are placed for the common core, but if the difference is in matters of the same genus as the named, then it is conventionally called ambiguous.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage opens a chapter on topics of words (مباحث الألفاظ), specifically defining the 'ambiguous' term (المشكك). The author explains that existence is an example: it is predicated of the Necessary Being with more perfection and priority, while of contingent beings with less. This makes it a term that causes doubt (شك) as to whether it is univocal (mutawati) or equivocal (mushtarak). Al-Dasooqi clarifies that the priority here is different from logical priority; it is about intensity and weakness. Examples are given: existence is more intense in the Necessary (eternal) than in the contingent (perishable), and similarly whiteness is more intense in snow than ivory, light in the sun than the moon. The gloss then explains why existence in the Necessary is 'more perfect' (it cannot be negated) and 'more prior' (it is identical to His essence). A reading variant of 'mushakkik' (active vs. passive participle) is noted, with the latter meaning 'causing doubt' and the former 'being doubted'. Ibn al-Tilimsani's objection is then presented: he claims that 'mushakkik' has no real meaning because if the difference is part of the meaning, the term is equivocal; if not, it is univocal. Al-Qarafi responds by preserving the category: both univocal and ambiguous terms refer to a common core, but when the difference is intrinsic to the named (e.g., existence differs in perfection), it is called ambiguous. This establishes the validity of the concept of tashkik in logic.

Key Terms
مشكك (mushakkik)
متواطئ (mutawati')
مشترك (mushtarak)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Qarafi, what distinguishes a mushakkik term from a mutawati term?
A) Mushakkik does not share a common core meaning.
B) Mushakkik has differences that are of the same genus as the named (like intensity).
C) Mushakkik has differences in the core meaning itself.
D) Mushakkik is a type of mushtarak.

Key Takeaway
The ambiguous term (mushakkik) is a valid logical category where instances share a core meaning but differ in degree, as defended by al-Qarafi against Ibn al-Tilimsani.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Consider the term 'iman' (faith). Is it a mushakkik term in Islamic theology? Justify your answer using the criteria from this lesson: identify the common core and the difference in intensity/perfection.
?

What Is Mantiq?
beginner
5 min
Distinguishing Univocal, Analogical, and Equivocal Words
Defines and distinguishes three types of words: univocal, analogical, equivocal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mutawat'ti, mushakkik, and mushtarak by applying their definitions to given examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
A word's meaning structure determines whether it is univocal, equivocal, or analogical.

This passage introduces a fundamental classification of words (alfaz) in Islamic logic. Understanding this classification is essential for precise reasoning, especially when analyzing terms used in Fiqh and Kalam. The three types—mutawat'ti (univocal), mushakkik (analogical), and mushtarak (equivocal)—differ in how their meanings relate to their instances. Here, the text explains mushakkik using the example of 'wujud' (existence) and then defines mushtarak as a word placed for each of its multiple meanings by a separate, original coinage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the word's meaning relationship
Determine whether the word applies to all its individuals with equal priority and intensity (mutawat'ti), with varying priority (mushakkik), or has multiple entirely distinct meanings (mushtarak).
2
Analyze the example of 'wujud'
The text gives existence as an example of mushakkik because it applies to God more perfectly and priorly than to creatures, causing doubt whether it is univocal or equivocal.
This shows how mushakkik sits between mutawat'ti and mushtarak.
3
Recognize the condition for mushtarak
A word is mushtarak only if each of its meanings is assigned by a separate, original act of coinage (wad' shakhsi), not by metaphorical extension.
This distinguishes mushtarak from words with multiple derived meanings.
4
Apply the test to an Islamic example
Consider the word 'riba' (usury). Does it have one core meaning applied with varying intensity, or multiple distinct meanings? Is it mutawat'ti, mushakkik, or mushtarak?
In Usul al-Fiqh, 'riba' is often treated as mushakkik because it applies to different transactions with varying degrees of prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مباحثِ الألفاظ. بأوليَّةٍ كما مرَّ ، وإما بأولوية كالوجودِ أيضاً، فإنَّه في الواجب أتم وأولى وتسميته بالمشكّكِ؛ لأنَّ النَّاظر فيه مشكك، هل هو متواطئ من حيثُ اتِّفاقُ أفراده في أصل المعنى، أو مشترك من حيثُ اختلافُ أفراده بالأولية أو غيرها؟! [ المشترك] (وَإِنْ كَثُرَ معناه) عطفٌ على قوله : «إنِ اتَّحد» ؛ أي: إن كَثُرَ معنى المفرد، فلا يخلو من أن يكون المفرد موضوعاً لكلِّ من المعاني الكثيرة أو لا . (فَإِنْ وُضِعَ) المفردُ (لِكُلٍّ) من المعاني الكثيرة؛ فَإِنْ وُضِعَ لكلِّ واحدٍ منها بوضع شخصي فالمشترك.
Chapter: On investigations of words. Either by priority as previously, or by priority like existence also, for it in the Necessary is more perfect and prior, and it is called mushakkik because the observer in it is doubtful: is it mutawat'ti in terms of agreement of its individuals in the root meaning, or mushtarak in terms of difference of its individuals by priority or other? [Mushtarak] (And if its meaning is many) is connected to His saying: 'if it is one'; meaning: if the meaning of the singular is many, then it is not free from the singular being placed for each of the many meanings or not. (So if) the singular (is placed for each) of the many meanings; if it is placed for each one of them by a personal placement, then it is mushtarak.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage opens a discussion on the classification of words (alfaz) in logic. It distinguishes three types: mutawat'ti (univocal), mushakkik (analogical/ambiguous), and mushtarak (equivocal). The text first explains mushakkik using the example of existence (wujud): existence is attributed to the Necessary Being (God) more perfectly and priorly than to contingent beings, causing doubt whether the word is univocal or equivocal. This leads to the definition of mushtarak: when a word has multiple meanings and is placed for each meaning by a separate, original placement (wad' shakhsi). The passage shows that the classification depends on whether the word is placed for a single common meaning (mutawat'ti), a meaning that applies with priority and intensity (mushakkik), or multiple distinct meanings (mushtarak). The commentator explains that mushtarak requires each meaning to be assigned by its own act of coinage, excluding metaphorical or transferred uses.

Key Terms
متواطئ
مشكك
مشترك

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of mushakkik given in the passage?
A) 'wujud' (existence)

Key Takeaway
The classification of words into mutawat'ti, mushakkik, and mushtarak is based on the relationship between a word and its meanings, which is critical for precise definition and argumentation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
